<div id="S0001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec-type_intro NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i3" class="section-heading-2">1. Introduction</h2>
 <p>Flow shop is a production system where all machines are organized based on operational jobs. Flow Shop Scheduling (FSS) problem involves determining an optimal schedule for jobs processing on machines and has been a research benchmark for many years. Optimization algorithms for two and three-machine flow shop problems have been developed in conjunction with different targets. As the majority of FSS problems are NP-hard; i.e., problems with non-polynomial run time, all of the exact, heuristic and meta-heuristic solution methods seek to minimize total completion time (makespan) (Chung, Flynn, &amp; Kirca, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0007" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2006</a></span>).</p>
 <p>There are three types of main objective functions for scheduling problems in flow shop system:</p>
 <ol class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-alpha-upper">
  <li><p class="inline">Based on jobs completion time,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Based on delivery time,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Based on the inventory and implementation cost of facilities/equipment.</p></li>
 </ol>
 <p></p>
 <p>There are various categories regarding completion time of jobs including all jobs completion time, average completion time, weighted completion time, and weighted average completion time (Khalili &amp; Tavakkoli-Moghaddam, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0016" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>).</p>
 <p>Other objective functions include total flow time, average flow time, weighted total flow time, weighted average flow time, maximum delay, total delay, average delay, maximum earliness, total earliness, average earliness, weighted average delay and completion time variance which have been examined in the recent literature (Xu &amp; Xiao, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0034" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2011</a></span>).</p>
 <p>One of the major issues in production planning is the optimal utilization of production resources; some of these resources are production machinery that should be exploited efficiently and effectively. On the other hand, there should always exist a significant volume of products and parts outside the production system as outsourcing is a necessary way to improve scheduling performance in various companies (Mokhtari &amp; Abadi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>; Qi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0023" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2011</a></span>). Moreover, it will cause manufacturers applying higher concentration on more important and more valuable issues in the workplace, this research focused on this issue. Nowadays many companies are outsourcing their jobs rather than implementing direct management process (Behnamian, Fatemi Ghomi, &amp; Zandieh, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0003" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>). Most of the manufacturers are faced with the conditions that demands exceed the capacity of production (Lee, Jeong, &amp; Moon, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0017" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2002</a></span>; Mokhtari &amp; Abadi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>). In this situation, they will outsource all or some of their jobs to a subcontractor or several subcontractors rather than design large amounts of productions or pay enormous costs of warehousing and inventory holding. Indeed, proper planning for outsourcing can reduce product delivery time and total costs as well as making the manufacturer plant more competitive. To achieve such benefits, managers have to make the decision about the amount of products to be produced and the amount of products to be outsourced (Mokhtari &amp; Abadi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>).</p>
 <p>One of the main aspects of this research is providing a solution for manufacturing companies that have a delay in delivering orders. The suggestion of this research is to divide jobs between themselves and their other subcontractors. This makes many orders executed in parallel between different production units. The main feature of this research is that it provides an optimal decision for between manufacturing firms to increase productivity as well as reduce the delay in the delivery of orders and increasing customers’ satisfaction.</p>
 <p>Therefore, this research presents an efficient mathematical model to minimize completion time and outsourcing costs by scheduling the in-house production and considering outsourcing option in addition to maintaining the integration of the problem. Furthermore, the model is developed using Robust Optimization (RO) method to cover the uncertain nature of the processing time parameter.</p>
 <p>The rest of the paper is organized as follows. <a href="#S0002">Section 2</a> reviews the relevant works in the literature. <a href="#S0003">Section 3</a> introduces the proposed RO formulation. The problem, mathematical model and its robust counterpart formulation are discussed in <a href="#S0004">Section 4</a>, and then <a href="#S0005">Section 5</a> presents the computational results including model validation, comparison results, and sensitivity analysis. <a href="#S0006">Section 6</a> provides a discussion of the obtained results of the research. Finally, conclusions and outlook of the research are described in <a href="#S0007">Section 7</a>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S0002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i4" class="section-heading-2">2. Literature review</h2>
 <p>Chung et al. (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0007" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2006</a></span>) applied a Branch-and-Bound algorithm for solving FSS problems of <i>m</i>-machine aiming at total tardiness minimization. They could demonstrate the efficiency of the proposed algorithm by conducting extensive computational experiments on test problems for less than 20 jobs. Naderi, Zandieh, Balagh, &amp; Roshanaei (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0021" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2009</a></span>) presented an improved Simulated Annealing (SA) algorithm for hybrid flow shops with sequence-dependent setup and transportation times to minimize total tardiness and maximum completion time. The proposed algorithm applies a Taguchi method to adjust algorithm parameters to reduce the frequency of testing. Khalili and Tavakkoli-Moghaddam (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0016" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>) proposed a bi-objective FSS problem with the aim of minimizing the maximum completion time and total weighted delay. In their study, it was assumed that there is no need for everything to be processed on all machines. Furthermore, the transportation time between stations is considered in the model. They developed a Multi-Objective Electromagnetic Algorithm (MOEM) to solve the problem. This algorithm applies the electromagnetic theory absorption and disposal mechanisms.</p>
 <p>Behnamian et al. (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0003" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>) introduced a hybrid meta-heuristic algorithm to solve a hybrid FSS problem with sequence-dependent preparation time that aims to minimization total earliness and delays. The algorithm includes three parts: 1) the first part generates a primary population using Ant Colony Optimization (ACO) algorithm, 2) the second part applies SA algorithm, and 3) the third part implements the local search to improve the solutions. (Liao &amp; Huang, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0018" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>) introduced three linear programming models for the non-permutation FSS problem with the objective function of minimizing all delays. They developed a Tabu Search (Bertsimas &amp; Sim, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>) algorithm to solve the problem.</p>
 <p>Some important research has been done in parallel machine environment considering different assumptions such as resource constraints (Hou, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0014" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>), sequence-dependent setup times (Hou, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0014" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>), machine eligibility constraint in automotive gear industry (Gokhale &amp; Mathirajan, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0009" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>), single batch delivery of production by vehicles in a supply chain (Cakici, Mason, Geismar, &amp; Fowler, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0006" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>), and acceptance or rejection possibility of jobs in order to minimize total penalty cost from rejections and make-span of accepted jobs (Zhang, Lu, &amp; Yuan, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0035" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2009</a></span>). Mokhtari and Abadi (Mokhtari &amp; Abadi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>) designed a Non-Linear Programming (NLP) model to solve a single-stage scheduling problem with outsourcing option with the aim of total cost minimization. It was assumed that subcontractors are capable to undertake all the outsourced jobs. They developed a heuristic algorithm to decompose the problem and solve them in a short run time.</p>
 <p>In uncertainty condition, Rahmani and Heydari (Rahmani &amp; Heydari, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0024" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>) developed a study of FSS problem to minimize the make-span, while maintaining stability and robustness, and incorporating uncertain processing times and the unexpected arrival of new jobs. Other production scheduling studies have included random processing times (Kamburowski, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0015" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2000</a></span>). Nagasawa, Ikeda, and Irohara (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0022" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2015</a></span>) presented a robust FSS problem with random processing time for reduction of peak power consumption. They used a scenario-based RO approach to implement randomness nature of the parameters.</p>
 <p>Recently, Fu, Ding, Wang, &amp; Wang (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0008" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>) developed a mathematical model for a flow-shop scheduling problem by considering multiple objectives, time-dependent processing time and uncertainty. They implemented a fireworks algorithm with some local search strategies to solve the problem. Brum and Ritt (Zhang et al., <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0035" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2009</a></span>) developed an algorithm with automatic configuration to solve the permutation FSS problem for minimizing total completion time. They investigated how algorithmic components can be combined to form a full heuristic search method. They compared their proposed methodology with several local search procedures in the literature to show its superiority.</p>
 <p>After reviewing the most contributed research, it is clarified that the previous works didn’t focus on the application of RO in the field of FSS with outsourcing option and just-in-time policy. Therefore, it can be concluded that studying robust just-in-time FSS with outsourcing option and considering due dates, resource constraints, and uncertain processing time on different machines is the main contribution of this research. As a consequence, this research focuses on several available suppliers to be selected for subcontracting and considers the scheduling of outsourced jobs as well as in-house in a flow shop system. Moreover, an RO approach based on Bertsimas and Sim (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>) is applied to the model to cope with the real world uncertain condition of the problem.</p>
</div>
<div id="S0003" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i5" class="section-heading-2">3. Robust optimization approach</h2>
 <p>Among existing approaches for dealing with uncertainty, RO is an efficient and reliable approach, which has been expanded to deal with uncertainty in recent years (Tirkolaee, Mahdavi, &amp; Esfahani, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0032" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018a</a></span>). In this approach, we look for solutions close to optimal which has a high possibility to be feasible. In other words, we can guarantee the feasibility of solutions while the optimality of the solutions is ignored. The aim of RO is to find a solution to show the least modifications against uncertainty.</p>
 <p>Generally, the robust models are divided into two groups (Xu &amp; Xiao, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0034" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2011</a></span>):</p>
 <ol class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-order">
  <li><p class="inline">The first group looks for a solution to optimize the objective function for the worst scenario.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">The second group imposes some conditions on solutions. In this way, a solution which can handle these imposing conditions is considered as a robust solution.</p></li>
 </ol>
 <p></p>
 <p>In fact, RO approach is a suitable method to create a primary plan so that the uncertainty of data leads to the least possible modifications. Mulvey, Vanderbei, and Zenios (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0020" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1995</a></span>) introduced an approach which combined the formulations of ideal programming with the scenarios of data. In the early 1970s, Soyster (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0026" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1973</a></span>) presented a linear optimization model that gives the best feasible solution for all input data so that each input data can get any value from an interval. This approach tends to find solutions, which are over-conservative. It means that for assuring the robustness of solutions in this approach, we get far from the optimization of the problem. Ben-Tal and Nemirovski (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0004" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1999</a></span>) presented an efficient algorithm for solving convex optimization problems under uncertainty of data assuming that data are uncertain in elliptic sets. While regarding the obtained robust formulations from the conic quadratic problem, these approaches cannot be implemented for discrete optimization problems. Bertsimas and Sim (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>) proposed a different technique to control the level of conservatism. This approach has the advantage of presenting a linear optimization model. Thus, it applies to discrete optimization models.</p>
 <p>Hence, for formulating the linear RO problems, we can apply several different approaches, which have been developed. Three main RO models and methods include Soyster (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0026" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1973</a></span>), Ben-Tal and Nemirovski (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0004" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1999</a></span>) and Bertsimas and Sim (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>). In this research, we implement Bertsimas’ and Sim’s model for formulating the problem due to its advantages (Tirkolaee, Goli, Bakhsi, &amp; Mahdavi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0029" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2017</a></span>).</p>
 <p>The procedure of the robust model development is described in the following.</p>
 <div id="S0003-S2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i6">3.1. Robust counterpart formulation</h3>

In other words, it is assumed that only one subset of the coefficients is allowed to affect the solution procedure undesirably (Bertsimas &amp; Sim, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2003</a></span>). With this assumption, it is guaranteed that if this happens naturally, our robust optimal solution will be strongly feasible. Moreover, regarding the symmetric distribution of variables, even if the number of changed coefficients exceeds <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>

     </mrow>
    </math></span>, optimal will remain feasible with a huge probability. Thus, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

    </math></span> is called the conservatism level for <i>i</i><sup>th</sup> constraint which ensures the robustness adjustment against the protection level of the solution (Tirkolaee et al., <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0029" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2017</a></span>).   <p><a href="#M0002">Equations. (2)</a>-(<a href="#M0004">4</a>) propose an NLP model so that the optimization is not guaranteed. To linearize this model, Theorem 1 is defined (Naderi et al., <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0021" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2009</a></span>). <statement content-type="theorem">
    (5) 
   </statement></p>
  <p><b>Theorem 1</b>: The conservation function of <i>i</i><sup>th</sup> constraint is calculated for the given vector of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

<div id="S0004" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i24" class="section-heading-2">4. Problem description and mathematical model</h2>
 <p>Problem description and the subsequent mathematical model development are the basis of the optimizations as we can survey in different types of optimization problems (Alinaghian, Amanipour, &amp; Tirkolaee, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0001" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>; Babaee Tirkolaee, Abbasian, Soltani, &amp; Ghaffarian, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0002" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>; Goli, Aazami, &amp; Jabbarzadeh, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0010" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Goli &amp; Davoodi, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0011" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Goli, Tirkolaee, Malmir, Bian, &amp; Sangaiah, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0012" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>; Hosseinabadi &amp; Tirkolaee, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0013" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Sangaiah, Tirkolaee, Goli, &amp; Dehnavi-Arani, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0025" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>; Tirkolaee, Alinaghian, Hosseinabadi, Sasi, &amp; Sangaiah, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0028" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Tirkolaee, Goli, Hematian, Sangaiah, &amp; Han, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0030" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>; Tirkolaee, Hosseinabadi, Soltani, Sangaiah, &amp; Wang, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0031" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Tirkolaee, Mahdavi, &amp; Esfahani, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0033" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018b</a></span>). The basic model of our proposed problem is a nonlinear programming model which has been presented in Mokhtari and Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>). Our proposed model develops the main model by considering job due date, availability of resources and uncertain processing time in addition to linearizing the model so that a novel RMILP model is designed.</p>
 <p>Each job <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0037.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msubsup>
     <mi>
      γ
     </mi>
     <mi>
      j
     </mi>
     <mi>
      k
     </mi>
    </msubsup>
   </math></span>. It is considered that some of these machines are stationed inside, and some of them are stationed outside of the manufacturer site as subcontractors. In this case, the inside jobs are considered with zero cost and the cost of the outsourced jobs is interpreted as the payments to the subcontractors. The other point is the consideration of completion time for the predetermined jobs. Considering the constraint of available resources inside the manufacturer plant may lead to an interaction between outsourcing and production in manufacturer plant in addition to cost and completion time factors.</p>
 <p>The model assumptions can be summarized as follows:</p>
 <ol class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-order">
  <li><p class="inline">The processing time of each job on each machine is assumed to be uncertain,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Each machine can process different jobs,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Split processing of jobs is not allowed (a job processing on a machine should not be divided into different operational time intervals),</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">All jobs are independent and available for processing at time zero,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Jobs setup time on machines are independent in sequences and has a given processing time,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">The processing cost of each job is a certain value.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Some of the manufacturing machines are assumed to be outside of the plant.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Outsourced jobs have a certain additional processing time, but they can be processed parallel with other inside jobs.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">The optimal scheduling should be non-delay scheduling as a just-in-time delivery policy.</p></li>
 </ol>
 <p></p>
 <p>Sets, indices, parameters, and variables of the problem are defined as below:</p>
 <div class="tableViewerArticleInfo hidden">
  <span class="figViewerTitle">A robust just-in-time flow shop scheduling problem with outsourcing option on subcontractors</span>

 <p>The objective function (18) represents the sum of total weighted completion time and total processing cost. <a href="#M0019">Equation. (19)</a> guarantees that each job is processed only once and <a href="#M0020">Equation. (20)</a> demonstrates that there is only one starting job to be processed on each machine. <a href="#M0021">Equation. (21)</a> plays the same role as flow conservation condition in network flow problems ensures that the jobs are correctly sequenced within a partial schedule on machine <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0049.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0049.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi>
     k
    </mi><mo>
     ∈
    </mo><mi>
     M
    </mi>
   </math></span> and also ensures that at most one job has to be the last job on the machine. <a href="#M0022">Equation. (22)</a> calculates the completion time <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0050.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0050.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>

       <mi>

       </mi>
      </mrow>
     </msub>

   </math></span> by considering the relationships between two adjacent jobs. <a href="#M0023">Equation. (23)</a> expresses that the completion time of job <i>j</i> should not exceed its due date. <a href="#M0024">Equation.  <p>In the following, it is attempted to schedule each machine using Smith’s rule (Goli et al., <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0012" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>). This rule states that in an optimal solution of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   <math>
    <mi>
     R
    </mi><mo>
     ∥
    </mo><msup>
     <mrow>
      <mo>

      </mo>
     </mrow>

 <p>Since the feasibility space of solutions decreased in problem <i>P’</i> (based on Smith rule), less computational time is needed to solve it. The above problem is a special kind of unrelated parallel machines with n jobs and <i>m</i>1+<i>m</i>2 machines. The structure of its objective function cannot be found in any scheduling problem of unrelated machines. <disp-formula-group id="M0029">

 <div id="S0004-S2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i41">4.1. Linearization of the model</h3>
  <p>As it is clear, <a href="#M0030">Equation. (30)</a> makes the model non-linear due to the multiplication of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0054.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0054.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <msubsup>
      <mi>
       x
      </mi>
      <mrow>
       <mi>
        i
       </mi>
       <mi>
        j
       </mi>
      </mrow>
      <mi>
       k
      </mi>
     </msubsup>
    </math></span> (a binary variable) by <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0055.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0055.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <msub>
       <mi>
        C
       </mi>
       <mrow>
        <mi>
         i
        </mi>
        <mi>
         k
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </mrow>
    </math></span> (a positive continuous variable) which occurs similarly to <a href="#M0022">Equation. (22)</a>. However, it can be linearized easily by defining a new variable of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0056.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0056.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <msubsup>
      <mi>
       h
      </mi>
      <mrow>
       <mi>
        i
       </mi>
       <mi>
        j
       </mi>
      </mrow>
      <mi>
       k
      </mi>
     </msubsup>
    </math></span> and applying <a href="#M0034">Equations. (34)</a> to (38) to the model instead of <a href="#M0030">Equation. (30)</a>. This would result in a mixed-integer linear programming (MILP) model. <disp-formula-group id="M0034">
    <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">

<div id="S0005" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i76" class="section-heading-2">5. Computational results</h2>
 <p>In this section, the applied steps for solving the proposed RMILP are explained.</p>
 <p><b>Step 1</b>: Based on Bertsimas and Sim approach, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0077.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0077.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi mathvariant="normal">
     Γ
    </mi>
   </math></span> (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0078.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0078.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mn>
     0
    </mn><mo>
     ≤
    </mo><mi mathvariant="normal">
     Γ
    </mi><mo>
     ≤
    </mo><mfenced open="|" close="|">
     <mi>
      j
     </mi>
    </mfenced><mo>
     ×
    </mo><mfenced open="|" close="|">
     <mi>
      k
     </mi>
    </mfenced>
   </math></span>) is determined for each <i>j</i> and each <i>k</i> in <a href="#M0045">Equation. (45)</a>. So it is considered to be (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0079.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0079.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mfenced open="|" close="|">
     <mi>
      j
     </mi>
    </mfenced><mo>
     ×
    </mo><mfenced open="|" close="|">
     <mi>
      k
     </mi>
    </mfenced>
   </math></span>)/2 as a golden mean.</p>
 <p><b>Step 2</b>: After choosing the value of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0080.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0080.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi mathvariant="normal">
     Γ
    </mi>
   </math></span>, the deviation value of the processing time is defined as <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0081.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0081.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mover>
     <mi>
      p
     </mi>
     <mo stretchy="false">
      ˆ
     </mo>
    </mover><mo>
     =
    </mo><mi>
     α
    </mi><mo>
     ×
    </mo><mi>
     p
    </mi>
   </math></span> (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0082.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0082.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi>
     α
    </mi>
   </math></span> is the predetermined parameter, namely, deviation value).</p>
 <p>In determining the amount of changed processing time, the below cases should be considered:</p>
 <ol class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-order">
  <li><p class="inline">If <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0083.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0083.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi>
     </math></span> is an integer, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0084.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0084.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi>
     </math></span> jobs should be chosen and the processing time should be increased.</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Otherwise, if <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0085.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0085.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi>
     </math></span> is not an integer, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0086.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0086.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi>
     </math></span> jobs are chosen for increasing the processing time. For <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0087.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0087.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi><mo>
       −
      </mo><mn>
       1
      </mn>
     </math></span> jobs, we act like case 1 and for the last job, the non-integer part is multiplied by the deviation value of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0088.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0088.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mover>
       <mi>
        p
       </mi>
       <mo stretchy="false">
        ˆ
       </mo>
      </mover>
     </math></span>, that is <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0089.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0089.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mrow>
       <msub>
        <mover>
         <mi>
          p
         </mi>
         <mo stretchy="false">
          ˆ
         </mo>
        </mover>
        <mrow>
         <mi>
          l
         </mi>
         <mi>

         </mi>

         <mi>

         </mi>
        </mrow>
       </msub>
      </mrow><mo>
       =
      </mo><mi>
       α
      </mi><mo>
       ×
      </mo><mo stretchy="false">
       (
      </mo><mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi>
     </math></span>-<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0090.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tpmr20/2019/tpmr20.v007.i01/21693277.2019.1620651/20191118/images/tpmr_a_1620651_ilm0090.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Γ
      </mi><mo stretchy="false">
       )
      </mo><mo>
       ×
      </mo><mi>
       p
      </mi>
     </math></span>.</p></li>
 </ol>
 <p></p>
 <p><b>Step 3</b>: We do this for all the processing jobs by machines in any solution to get the new matrix of processing time.</p>
 <p><b>Step 4</b>: After applying Steps 1 to 3, the robust solution is achieved.</p>
 <div id="S0005-S2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i77">5.1. Design of experiments</h3>
  <p>In this section, some instance problems are generated randomly to study the efficiency and verification of the proposed model and also to evaluate the effects of robustness. Fifteen scenarios including random instance problems are designed in different sizes. The information of the problems is given in <button class="ref showTableEventRef" data-id="T0001">Table 1</button>. The input parameters are generated uniformly.   <p>It should be noted that problem 6 is regarded as a real case of Teram Chap Company which is one of the pioneers of printing and packaging industry in Iran, especially in box manufacturing (Teram Industrial Group, <span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0027" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>). The most demanded products include luxury, chocolate boxes, beverages and food boxes, cosmetics, and pharmaceutical packaging boxes. The problem is studied for processing 20 chosen jobs on 3 in-house machines and 3 possible subcontractors to produce chocolate and food boxes. The values of the input parameters have been assigned based on the experts of the company.</p>
  <p>Initially, both deterministic and robust models are solved using data given in <button class="ref showTableEventRef" data-id="T0001">Table 1</button>. CPLEX solver of GAMS software version 23.6 is used to solve the model by a laptop of Intel Core i7, (8 GB RAM). Furthermore, a runtime limitation of 3600 is implemented to report the obtained solution. The computational results are shown in <button class="ref showTableEventRef" data-id="T0002">Table 2</button>. The results of solving the robust counterpart problem are represented for the deviation levels of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

  <p><a href="#F0001">Figure 1</a> shows the differences between objective function values of deterministic and robust problems. As we can see, these differences are more tangible in large-sized problems. In fact, it has been clear that the value of the processing time plays an important role in making this difference. Managers should pay careful attention to these different deviation levels of processing times that have a direct impact on the objective and make it worse when increase.</p>

  <p></p>
  <p><a href="#F0002">Figure 2</a> depicts the reported run times up to 3600 seconds. As it is obvious, run time value in the robust problems is higher than deterministic problems. It demonstrates that the robust problem adds more complexity to the problem. Moreover, we can conclude that robust problems have a worse objective function due to its effort to generate a feasible solution in different uncertain conditions that will be done by imposing additional costs.</p>

 <div id="S0005-S2002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i80">5.2. Sensitivity analysis</h3>
  <p>In this section, a sensitivity analysis is performed on <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   <div class="figureFootNote-F0003"></div>
  </div>
  <p></p>
  <p>According to <a href="#F0003">Figure 3</a>, we can find that objective function value will be reduced relatively by decreasing the demand and similarly increases against demand reduction with different rates of change. We can conclude that the objective value has approximately a linear relation with the demand parameter. Thus, we can achieve an optimal strategy concerning the demand level control and by considering a tradeoff between in-house production and outsourcing based on different conditions.</p>
 </div>
 <div id="S0005-S2003" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i82">5.3. Results comparison with Other solution techniques</h3>
  <p>Since the proposed model is an extended model of the previous one in the literature which was introduced by Mokhtari and Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>), a comparison is conducted to evaluate the superiority of our model. To this end, the applied solutions techniques for the proposed NLP model in the previous research including LINGO and Lagrangian method are considered to investigate the advantages and disadvantages of our deterministic MILP model. Six instances problems extracted from Mokhtari and Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>) are studied and the comparison results are represented in <button class="ref showTableEventRef" data-id="T0004">Table 4</button>. It should be noted that our suggested MILP model is solved without capacity limitation of available resources (which was not studied in Mokhtari and Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>)) and without the 3600 runtime limitation. The run time limitation is set to 12 h for the comparison of CPLEX with LINGO according to Mokhtari &amp; Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>).</p>
  <div class="tableViewerArticleInfo hidden">
   <span class="figViewerTitle">A robust just-in-time flow shop scheduling problem with outsourcing option on subcontractors</span>
   <div class="articleAuthors articleInfoSection">
    <div class="authorsHeading">
     All authors
    </div>
    <div class="authors">
     <a class="entryAuthor" href="/action/doSearch?Contrib=Goli%2C+Alireza"><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor"></span></a><a href="/author/Goli%2C+Alireza"><span class="NLM_given-names">Alireza</span> Goli</a> <a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0001-9535-9902"><img src="/templates/jsp/images/orcid.png"></a>, <a class="entryAuthor" href="/action/doSearch?Contrib=Babaee+Tirkolaee%2C+Erfan"><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor"></span></a><a href="/author/Babaee+Tirkolaee%2C+Erfan"><span class="NLM_given-names">Erfan</span> Babaee Tirkolaee</a> <a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-1664-9210"><img src="/templates/jsp/images/orcid.png"></a> &amp; <a class="entryAuthor" href="/action/doSearch?Contrib=Soltani%2C+Mehdi"><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor"></span></a><a href="/author/Soltani%2C+Mehdi"><span class="NLM_given-names">Mehdi</span> Soltani</a>
    </div>
   </div>
   <div class="articleLowerInfo articleInfoSection">
    <div class="articleLowerInfoSection articleInfoDOI">
     <a href="https://doi.org/10.1080/21693277.2019.1620651">https://doi.org/10.1080/21693277.2019.1620651</a>
    </div>

     <h6>Published online:</h6>28 May 2019
    </div>
   </div>
  </div>
  <div class="tableView">
   <div class="tableCaption">
    <div class="short-legend">
     <h3><p class="captionText"><span class="captionLabel">Table 4. </span> Results comparison of CPLEX with the techniques proposed by Mokhtari &amp; Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>).</p></h3>
    </div>
   </div>
   <div class="tableDownloadOption" data-hascsvlnk="true" id="T0004-table-wrapper">
    <a class="downloadButton btn btn-sm" role="button" href="/action/downloadTable?id=T0004&amp;doi=10.1080%2F21693277.2019.1620651&amp;downloadType=CSV"> Download CSV</a><a data-id="T0004" class="downloadButton btn btn-sm displaySizeTable" href="#" role="button">Display Table</a>
   </div>
  </div>
  <p></p>
  <p>As can be seen in <button class="ref showTableEventRef" data-id="T0004">Table 4</button>, our proposed model and solver could yield better results compared to the NLP model of Mokhtari and Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>) in terms of Q-gap and runtime. In fact, our MILP model is solved exactly within remarkable lower runtimes by CPLEX. However, a Lagrangian heuristic could find good solutions within lower runtimes than CPLEX and LINGO. <a href="#F0004">Figure 4</a> depicts the run time comparisons.</p>

<div id="S0006" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i85" class="section-heading-2">6. Discussion</h2>
 <p>The numerical results showed that the uncertainty yields a situation with more complexity and higher total cost. Furthermore, it made the model more complicated to be solved in comparison with the deterministic model. It has been found that the objective function values and the run time values are bigger in the robust problems of 1–15. In the real world condition, managers are faced with uncertainty and need to provide an overview of decision-making processes in these different uncertain conditions. For this purpose, as a real case example in Teram Chap Company, the proposed methodology provided comparing results for both deterministic and robust problem to show the behavior of the objective value. On the other hand, a sensitivity analysis was performed on the parameter of demand for in-house production resources to evaluate the objective behavior alternatively. According to this proposed methodology, it was revealed that the robust problem with the uncertainty level of 0.1 makes a significant increase in total cost in comparison with the deterministic problem. However, the next increase in the uncertainty level of 0.2 is not as large as it is and these differences become more remarkable with the increase of the problem size. This happens also in sensitivity analysis result so that the objective value changes from the robust problem with the uncertainty level of 0.2 to the robust problem with the uncertainty level of 0.1 is smaller than the objective value changes from the robust problem with the uncertainty level of 0.1 to the deterministic problem.</p>
 <p>Moreover, the final comparison analysis between our MILP model and the proposed NLP model by Mokhtari and Abadi (<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i87" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2013</a></span>) demonstrated that CPLEX can generate high-quality solutions in comparison with LINGO and Lagrangian method, however, the Lagrangian method is able to find near-optimal solutions within lower run times.</p>
 <p>As a great achievement, the results of this research may be considered as an applicable managerial tool to help them in the decision-making process under uncertainty.</p>
</div>
<div id="S0007" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i86" class="section-heading-2">7. Conclusion and outlook</h2>
 <p>Scheduling problem is one of the most well-known issues in production system studies. Due to the increasing importance of on-time delivery of jobs to the customers, this paper suggests a single-stage just-in-time production-scheduling model with an option of outsourcing. The goal of the problem is to find the optimal sequence of jobs for each machine. To analyze more real word assumptions, the due date of jobs and resource capacity constraint are studied in the model. Moreover, the uncertain nature of processing time is evaluated by the robust optimization approach. The proposed methodology is validated by generating and solving 15 different-sized instance problems. The results show that uncertain jobs processing time lead to having different solutions compared to the deterministic problem, and these differences mostly increase machines and outsourcing to the subcontractors. Then, in the sensitivity analysis, the importance of the processing cost parameter on objective function values in deterministic and robust problems is studied. Finally, the superiority of our proposed MILP was tested compared to the other solution techniques in the literature.</p>
 <p>For future works, the following suggestions may be considered:</p>
 <ul class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-bullet">
  <li><p class="inline">Adding a planning horizon into the model such as a weekly periodic scheduling model,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Studying other objective functions such as reliability maximization of scheduling,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Applying other methods to deal with uncertainty such as stochastic programming,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">Developing efficient meta-heuristics to solve the large-sized problems in a reasonable run time.</p></li>
 </ul>
 <p></p>
</div>
